  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e92a032f-934f-4183-8c66-d5bba5231b9e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText8560758189092862232" style="display:none"><b>Three weeks. Two sisters. One car. A True Story</b><br /><br />Raina can’t wait to be a big sister. But once Amara is born, things aren’t quite how she expected them to be. Amara is cute, but she’s also a cranky, grouchy baby, and mostly prefers to play by herself. Their relationship doesn’t improve much over the years, but when a baby brother enters the picture and later, when something doesn’t seem right between their parents, they realize they must figure out how to get along. They are sisters, after all.<br /><br />Raina uses her signature humor and charm in both present-day narrative and perfectly placed flashbacks to tell the story of her relationship with her sister, which unfolds during the course of a road trip from their home in San Francisco to a family reunion in Colorado.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=real-life-matters">real-life-matters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1020107956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5265163394530290209">Raina and Amara's relationship:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407455492ra/10725041.gif' width='500' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is a companion novel to Smile, which I really liked and absolutely recommend. What is great about these works is that they’re based on true events that the author herself lived when she was a teenager.<br/><br/>It’s mainly about her (Raina) and her sister’s (Amara) relationship and how they overcome their differences, given that they both have different personalities and centers of interest - and this is bound to create tensions.<br/><br/>The plot isn't extremely complex, and it </span>
  <span id="freeText5265163394530290209" style="display:none">Raina and Amara's relationship:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407455492ra/10725041.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a companion novel to Smile, which I really liked and absolutely recommend. What is great about these works is that they’re based on true events that the author herself lived when she was a teenager.<br><br>It’s mainly about her (Raina) and her sister’s (Amara) relationship and how they overcome their differences, given that they both have different personalities and centers of interest - and this is bound to create tensions.<br><br>The plot isn't extremely complex, and it does feel familiar, but in my opinion this is where its charm comes from, seeing that it's very easy to understand what we see and connect with the characters because this is something many of us have experienced before. <br><br>Raina is a character you will easily love and her sister one you will easily despise. At first, at least. She was a monster when she was younger, but in many ways cute and funny. Luckily, she undergoes a noticeable character development.<br><br>When I was a kid, I kept wanting a sister to play with, exactly like Raina. I wanted to share the kind of relationship we see sisters share on TV, for example in the Charmed TV show (which is one of my favourites). Well, I only ever had my brother. But that's okay, since regardless of the fights we have, I wouldn’t switch my brother for a sister. Ever.<br><br>This graphic novel will appeal to a lot of readers, especially children and people who want to read a cute family-themed story. Very recommended.<br><br><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5265163394530290209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer738876420597566930">Telgemeier's books just keep getting better and better in my eyes. My third read, <strong>Sisters</strong>, in particular resonated with me because of the main notion of sisterhood and its complications/ joys. Also, shoutout to my local library for holding a copy of this graphic novel. I initially picked it up for my little sister, but ended up enjoying it myself in one sitting just before she came home from school.<br/><br/>Raina uses her signature humor and charm in both present-day narrative and perfectly placed flashb</span>
  <span id="freeText738876420597566930" style="display:none">Telgemeier's books just keep getting better and better in my eyes. My third read, <strong>Sisters</strong>, in particular resonated with me because of the main notion of sisterhood and its complications/ joys. Also, shoutout to my local library for holding a copy of this graphic novel. I initially picked it up for my little sister, but ended up enjoying it myself in one sitting just before she came home from school.<br><br>Raina uses her signature humor and charm in both present-day narrative and perfectly placed flashbacks to tell the story of her relationship with her sister, which unfolds during the course of a road trip from their home in San Francisco to a family reunion in Colorado.<br><br>I was incredibly pumped to see what my little sister would think about this read, since it's the perfect visual example of what I felt like during those years before her birth. The whole notion of nagging and begging your mom for a little sister really resonated with me. And then, funnily enough, when the baby finally (and thankfully) arrives, you're hit with the realization that newborns can't play with you just yet.<br><br>Another note I loved was the combination of road trips with family and summer vibes thrown in here. Oh, and the art!! We have tons of stunning visuals on a wide range of colors. And I still don’t have the vocabulary to explain how great it is, so here are some examples:<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer13309175484374364629">This is a review with my daughter, who got this book from her school library. She chose 4 stars because she "really liked it." She thought it was funny. Her favorite character was Amara. One of her favorite scenes was when they got the snake. :)<br/><br/>She is not really big on reading (YET). <div id="review_1252226937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1252226937" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1252226937?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545540599" href="/book/show/18225809-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=middle-grade-or-childrens">middle-grade-or-childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1252226937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7138386192586063738"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br/><br/>Raina and Amara are sisters. Raina used to beg her parents for a younger sister, until one day she finally got her wish. From almost day one the two are polar opposites and do not get along very well. As the family goes on a road trip to Colorado, Raina flashes back to memories of growing up, giving back story on the complicated and sometimes frustrating relationship between the two girls. But although the two do not get along, they begin to try and compromise, because they are famil</span>
  <span id="freeText7138386192586063738" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br /><br />Raina and Amara are sisters. Raina used to beg her parents for a younger sister, until one day she finally got her wish. From almost day one the two are polar opposites and do not get along very well. As the family goes on a road trip to Colorado, Raina flashes back to memories of growing up, giving back story on the complicated and sometimes frustrating relationship between the two girls. But although the two do not get along, they begin to try and compromise, because they are family.<br /><br />This is a book easily devoured in one sitting. For a subject such as sibling dynamics it is wildly entertaining, and I found myself chuckling quite a few times. The plot is very basic yet works extremely well; the sibling dynamic is what makes the book so funny even if the reader doesn’t have a sister. The graphics are really well done, some of them more detailed than others but all wonderful. <br /><br />Told from the perspective of Raina, it’s easy for the reader to find Amara incredibly annoying, although at times I felt really bad for her because she seemed to be misunderstood and had a very difficult time expressing herself in a calm way. It was nice to see a family dynamic and how certain events affect the family as a whole, such as the father losing his job and how the children react to it. There was also the added maybe of the parents leaning toward a divorce which was never explicitly cleared up and it would have been nice to know if they were. <br /><br />This is a book that can be enjoyed by all ages, and a very quick and fun read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7138386192586063738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1137154378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1137154378" />
    <a title="Idarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah"><img alt="Idarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596863879p2/1283951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137154378?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Idarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Idarah" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah">Idarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137154378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13864443810896268944">I've been waiting for the publication of this book since I read Telgemeier's previous graphic novel <i>Smile</i>. This one picks up soon after the previous book, and centers around a family road trip from San Francisco through the Colorado Rockies for a family reunion. Throughout the book, Telgemeier sheds light on the complicated relationship between herself and her younger sister, Amara, which is sort of hinted at in the earlier book.<br/><br/>I especially liked how the author was able to journey back from pre</span>
  <span id="freeText13864443810896268944" style="display:none">I've been waiting for the publication of this book since I read Telgemeier's previous graphic novel <i>Smile</i>. This one picks up soon after the previous book, and centers around a family road trip from San Francisco through the Colorado Rockies for a family reunion. Throughout the book, Telgemeier sheds light on the complicated relationship between herself and her younger sister, Amara, which is sort of hinted at in the earlier book.<br /><br />I especially liked how the author was able to journey back from present to past using different colored panel backgrounds in order to lay the groundwork for the two sisters. Like I said before, I just really, really admire Telgemeier's art style. In its own way, it's a modern twist on a vintage style of comics. Add to that the fact that this series is autobiographical, it is such a unique way to share family history. I highly recommend it to everyone!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13864443810896268944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1043723493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1043723493" />
    <a title="Erica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2644090-erica"><img alt="Erica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558548351p2/2644090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1043723493?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica" href="/user/show/2644090-erica">Erica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545540599" href="/book/show/18225809-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=growing-up">growing-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=mothers-and-their-kids">mothers-and-their-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=sisters">sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=women-and-girls">women-and-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=travel">travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=jf">jf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=colorado">colorado</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1043723493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6001013236872499295">Wow.<br/>I love this story so much, it almost makes me cry.<br/>Almost.<br/><br/>It's a simple story. A mom, her two daughters and one son drive from San Francisco to Colorado Springs for a family reunion. Dad flies out separately.<br/><br/>There's road tripping and camping, something predominant in my own childhood. There's family fighting, there's a Walkman, there are Strawberry Shortcake dolls and cousins who are too cool and too many little children running around. There's a rogue snake and Dinosaur National Monument. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText6001013236872499295" style="display:none">Wow.<br />I love this story so much, it almost makes me cry.<br />Almost.<br /><br />It's a simple story. A mom, her two daughters and one son drive from San Francisco to Colorado Springs for a family reunion. Dad flies out separately.<br /><br />There's road tripping and camping, something predominant in my own childhood. There's family fighting, there's a Walkman, there are Strawberry Shortcake dolls and cousins who are too cool and too many little children running around. There's a rogue snake and Dinosaur National Monument. There's the tension between sisters as one grows up but the other matures, as one gets her own room and the other gets stuck with the little brother, as one tunes out the world and the other is overwhelmed by all the things in the world.<br /><br />I recognized everything. Every little thing. I'll bet I could even find the house in Colorado Springs where Aunt Mary and cousin Lindsey lived.<br /><br />This is a middle grade (juvenile) graphic novel about a girl who is in the summer between middle school and high school, who is bothered by her family, and who doesn't really pay attention to what's going on around her. It's also about her sister.<br />Despite it taking place in the late 80's and early 90's, it's still accessible to people in this stage of transition as well as to oldest and middle siblings. It would probably be pretty enjoyable to their parents, too.<br /><br />If my sister were on Goodreads, I'd recommend this to her. Actually, I'll probably just buy her a copy. She'll love it as much as I.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6001013236872499295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2479034255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2479034255" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2479034255?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-middle-grade">bage-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=comics-graphic-novel">comics-graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-coming-of-age">genre-coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=award-goodreads-choice">award-goodreads-choice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=women">women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=z-raina-telgemeier">z-raina-telgemeier</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2479034255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11295137472462281185">I love Raina's work. Smile and Sisters is fantastic; both are memoirs in nature. This is about siblings and family dynamics. I keep telling my niece to be nice to her younger brother; you never know if one day you will be living in his basement. I have to admit that I did not treat my brother well as a child. Someone, he got over it and we get along pretty well now. I live in his basement while I go to school. I am grateful. <br/><br/>The story is also a road trip. They drive from CA to CO. Crazy.<br/><br/>I love t</span>
  <span id="freeText11295137472462281185" style="display:none">I love Raina's work. Smile and Sisters is fantastic; both are memoirs in nature. This is about siblings and family dynamics. I keep telling my niece to be nice to her younger brother; you never know if one day you will be living in his basement. I have to admit that I did not treat my brother well as a child. Someone, he got over it and we get along pretty well now. I live in his basement while I go to school. I am grateful. <br /><br />The story is also a road trip. They drive from CA to CO. Crazy.<br /><br />I love the cheerful art. Raina seems to be honest in her depictions of family life. I'm sure there is exaggeration in there and story telling. It is well done and I am good and entertained.<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText2533290209423510404" style="display:none">I need to learn how to post a picture here from Dropbox but on the iPad. If I can post it, there will be no words required for my review because it is artwork my daughter had done for a school project. She chose this book because she is inspired by Raina Telgemeir and after reading this, it is easy to see why. This graphic memoir includes real issues that affect everyone: sibling rivalry, how age gaps affect the sibling relationship, parental conflict, and my personal favorite...fear of snakes. A fun, often funny look at the evolution of the relationship between two sisters presented through engaging illustrations and with a king snake thrown in! Raina Telgemeir owns this market. 4 stars</span>

<div id="review_2921568649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2921568649" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2921568649?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=z-2019-reads">z-2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=graphic-novels-manga-comics">graphic-novels-manga-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2921568649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7794215580425220941">I loved <i>Smile</i> so much a few weeks ago that I rushed to pick up <i>Sisters</i> from the library, too; sadly, though, this one was pretty disappointing in comparison. It's not a bad read by any means (as you can see, I still gave it a pretty neutral rating), but I feel that its storyline is extremely weak compared to its predecessor.<br/><br/>To be fair, maybe it's one of those "it's the reader, not the book" moments happening here because I don't have siblings and can't relate to the struggles of sisterhood — but</span>
  <span id="freeText7794215580425220941" style="display:none">I loved <i>Smile</i> so much a few weeks ago that I rushed to pick up <i>Sisters</i> from the library, too; sadly, though, this one was pretty disappointing in comparison. It's not a bad read by any means (as you can see, I still gave it a pretty neutral rating), but I feel that its storyline is extremely weak compared to its predecessor.<br /><br />To be fair, maybe it's one of those "it's the reader, not the book" moments happening here because I don't have siblings and can't relate to the struggles of sisterhood — but to be fair, books like this would have only reinforced how much I loved being an only child, had I read this as a kid. These two are so awful to each other and the only resolution found at the ending is minor and bittersweet. I didn't enjoy reading about them being at each other's throats the entire time and found the whole story to be pretty bland. A little too "slice of life" for me, I suppose.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7794215580425220941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2433273790" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2433273790" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2433273790?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22058361-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=families">families</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-history-nonfiction">childrens-history-nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=biographies-memoirs">biographies-memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=sibling-rivalry">sibling-rivalry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2433273790&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2433273790" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18121493114238147324">Now while I have massively appreciated Raina Telegemeier's autobiographical <u>Sisters</u> (and have once again been very pleasantly surprised at how much I have actually managed to find reading pleasure in a graphic novel, as that has truly only very recently started being the case for me), I also have to admit that I have definitely and truly found <u>Sisters</u> as often hitting way way too close to home for me and being almost uncannily spot on in almost every way regarding Raina's often problematic, some</span>
  <span id="freeText18121493114238147324" style="display:none">Now while I have massively appreciated Raina Telegemeier's autobiographical <u>Sisters</u> (and have once again been very pleasantly surprised at how much I have actually managed to find reading pleasure in a graphic novel, as that has truly only very recently started being the case for me), I also have to admit that I have definitely and truly found <u>Sisters</u> as often hitting way way too close to home for me and being almost uncannily spot on in almost every way regarding Raina's often problematic, sometimes downright nasty relationship with her younger sister Amara. <br /><br />And yes, while with <u>Sisters</u>, I could therefore relate more than one hundred percent and on an intensely personal and emotional level to Raina and Amara's squabbles and oh so many differences of opinion and views on life, I also have not really all that much been able to totally de-stress and enjoy my reading time (and indeed with the comic book illustrations also my viewing time) of <u>Sisters</u> as I have in fact and actually been continually confronted with and by an often painful and tense sibling relationship that has frustratingly and sadly generally been like a total and almost frighteningly exact mirror image of my own often fraught, dysfunctional relationship with my younger sister (except to say that while in <u>Sisters</u>, at the end of the story, when Amara and Raina are stranded in the desert waiting for their mother to return with help after their car breaks down, they do come to more of an understanding and appreciation of one another, my sister and I even now are still so different that we might as well be inhabiting different planets). <br /><br />A graphic novel about family relationships and dysfunction is <u>Sisters</u>, with Raina Telgemeier realistically but also sometimes with considerable humour showing that yes indeed, siblings often do not mesh, that siblings can be royal pains in the behind (and I do say that even about myself), that even in close and loving families, there can be a myriad of both problems and seemingly insurmountable differences of personalty, philosophy and emotionality. And yes, I have thus both loved and also indeed at times totally hated and despised <u>Sisters</u> (but even with my occasional fury and bitterness, <u>Sisters</u> is still and totally a five star ranking for me, for as already mentioned above, the one main and really the only reason for my occasional but massive annoyance and frustration is the simple fact that <u>Sisters</u> is just too personally relatable, too realistic at times to be a comforting or relaxing, soothing reading experience).</span>
  <a data-text-id="18121493114238147324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1131704042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1131704042" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1131704042?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=friend-recommended">friend-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=comics-and-graphic-novel">comics-and-graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1131704042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1610926127541516124">Do you remember how it feels to spend a long road trip in the car, arguing with your sibling? Telgemeier has been kind enough to document that for the reader, so any time you feel like remembering the many arguments over being hot, or someone kicking your seat, or how bored you were, you can just open up this graphic novel and be reminded of fun times when parents determined when you could pee and eat. Yay.<br/><br/>This made it to my TBR through some friends' reviews and by virtue of being a big sister m</span>
  <span id="freeText1610926127541516124" style="display:none">Do you remember how it feels to spend a long road trip in the car, arguing with your sibling? Telgemeier has been kind enough to document that for the reader, so any time you feel like remembering the many arguments over being hot, or someone kicking your seat, or how bored you were, you can just open up this graphic novel and be reminded of fun times when parents determined when you could pee and eat. Yay.<br /><br />This made it to my TBR through some friends' reviews and by virtue of being a big sister myself. I was hoping Tegemeier's autobiographical work might give some insight into that relationship. The answer is both yes-and-no; this is more a slice-of-life depiction rather than any introspective piece ala Roz Chast and her graphic book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18594409.Can_t_We_Talk_about_Something_More_Pleasant_" title="Can't We Talk about Something More Pleasant? by Roz Chast" rel="nofollow noopener">Can't We Talk about Something More Pleasant?</a>. Sisters is about Amara and her family, and the summer they took a road trip from their home in San Francisco to a family reunion in Colorado. The story is interrupted by flashbacks from a wide variety of time periods through the girls' earlier lives, largely showing how Raina and her little sister Amara are essentially two little people with very different predilections and goals.<br /><br />The drawings are solidly done, in a semi-realistic style. It's very easy to tell all the characters apart and it's nice they are all proportional.<br /><br />I give credit to Telgemeier for writing and drawing with total frankness and not sparing her adolescent self from the lens. Both sisters are clearly suffering at times and are crossing swords due to frustration. The road trip--of course--gives them an opportunity to go through a funny hardship together. It ends on a very mixed note, including potential big family changes that are never resolved, but with the sisters reaching a temporary alliance.<br /><br />Ultimately, a miss, mostly because it is too on target with the conflict without bringing much of a gestalt out of it. Two and a half slug-bugs, rounding up because it's mostly me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1610926127541516124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1036978152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036978152" />
    <a title="Liviania" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania"><img alt="Liviania" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218840926p2/1430644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1036978152?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liviania" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liviania" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania">Liviania</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545749510" href="/book/show/17801394-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036978152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13265140831955387805">Raina Telgemeier's SMILE is hugely successful, critically acclaimed, and basically everyone was excited when news of a companion graphic memoir broke. SISTERS is about (surprise surprise) Raina's relationship with her sister Amara. Raina wished for a sister, but the reality wasn't quite what she hoped.<br/><br/>SISTERS moves smoothly back and forth in time, the borders of the panels helping mark flashbacks. The bulk of the action takes place on a family road trip to Colorado. Raina, Amara, their mother, a</span>
  <span id="freeText13265140831955387805" style="display:none">Raina Telgemeier's SMILE is hugely successful, critically acclaimed, and basically everyone was excited when news of a companion graphic memoir broke. SISTERS is about (surprise surprise) Raina's relationship with her sister Amara. Raina wished for a sister, but the reality wasn't quite what she hoped.<br /><br />SISTERS moves smoothly back and forth in time, the borders of the panels helping mark flashbacks. The bulk of the action takes place on a family road trip to Colorado. Raina, Amara, their mother, and brother are all in a car (kind of old and broken down), while their father is flying. Between each "present" section is a flashback to the family growing - sister, brother, pets, and all that comes with.<br /><br />Some of the darker developments might surprise younger readers, but the astute ones will catch on to some of the underlying family tensions. At the same time, SISTERS is just as charming and cheerful as expected. Raina and Amara's combative relationship will be familiar to anyone with a sibling - as will their moment(s) of detente.<br /><br />As always, Telgemeier's art is expressive, albeit deceptively simple. It's very easy to follow and well laid out, perfect for readers new to or familiar with graphic novels. There have been no radical changes in style; why change what works?<br /><br />SISTERS is a slightly looser work than SMILE in addition to being slightly more mature. It is an excellent companion. I enjoy Telgemeier's fiction too, but she does a terrific job of mining her own life for story. The events of sisters are mundane, but the telling is funny and affecting. SISTERS is sure to please Telgemeier's many fans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13265140831955387805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1003229741" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1003229741" />
    <a title="Steph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5428996-steph"><img alt="Steph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514946855p2/5428996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1003229741?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph" href="/user/show/5428996-steph">Steph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545749510" href="/book/show/17801394-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5428996-steph?shelf=first-read-in-2014">first-read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5428996-steph?shelf=bio-memoir">bio-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5428996-steph?shelf=giveaways-arcs">giveaways-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5428996-steph?shelf=summertime-sadness">summertime-sadness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5428996-steph?shelf=graphic-comic-manga">graphic-comic-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5428996-steph?shelf=ebook-laptop">ebook-laptop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1003229741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15799421945366392337">I am really impressed by this book - <i>Sisters</i> strikes a perfect balance between adorably cute and solemnly heartfelt. Telgemeier’s art is wonderful, and her story is strong. <i>Sisters</i> captures the difficulty of being a kid, and the frustrations and joys of family. It’s funny and it’s sweet and it’s poignant - I highly recommend <i>Sisters.</i><br/><br/><i>Thank you to NetGalley and Scholastic for providing me with a copy of this book in return for an honest review.</i></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074260549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1962323135791301961">This is a companion to Telgemeier's wonderful <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6393631.Smile__Smile___1_' title='Smile (Smile, #1) by Raina Telgemeier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Smile</a>, in that it's also about her life. You could very easily read either book without ever having to read the other, but why would you want to do that? They're both great.<br/><br/>Sisters, naturally enough, is about Raina's relationship with her younger sister Amara, from Amara's birth through Raina's teens. And as a big sister, I can so completely and totally relate. Nobody can push your buttons like a younger sibling. Trust me, my sister actually and lite</span>
  <span id="freeText1962323135791301961" style="display:none">This is a companion to Telgemeier's wonderful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6393631.Smile__Smile___1_" title="Smile (Smile, #1) by Raina Telgemeier" rel="nofollow noopener">Smile</a>, in that it's also about her life. You could very easily read either book without ever having to read the other, but why would you want to do that? They're both great.<br /><br />Sisters, naturally enough, is about Raina's relationship with her younger sister Amara, from Amara's birth through Raina's teens. And as a big sister, I can so completely and totally relate. Nobody can push your buttons like a younger sibling. Trust me, my sister actually and literally in a very real sense scarred me for life. She was a biter. Anyways. Raina does a great job with showing just how difficult the relationship between siblings can be, and she does it without sparing herself. Yes, Amara is often difficult in this book, but Raina is, too. True, Amara does come off a little better through most of the book, but this is filtered through her own memories. I'm sure it must have been very, very tempting to make herself look better. <br /><br />This is definitely in Raina's signature style: cartoony, simple, expressive. I like it, it's clean, and it works for what she's doing here. But it is very simple, and verges on plain in spots. Not enough to bother me, but something to keep in mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1962323135791301961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_942904170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/942904170" />
    <a title="Tasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/929521-tasha"><img alt="Tasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448392221p2/929521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/942904170?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tasha" href="/user/show/929521-tasha">Tasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545749510" href="/book/show/17801394-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/929521-tasha?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/929521-tasha?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer942904170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2600364945225391301">The exceptionally talented and incredibly popular Raina Telgemeier returns with a sequel to her beloved Smile. This is the story of Raina and her little sister, Amara. Raina was desperate to have a little sister, but Amara is not working out the way she had pictured. Now Raina is stuck on a road trip with her sister, little brother and her mother. They are all stuck in a van traveling from San Francisco to Colorado for a family reunion. The relationship between the two sisters is tense, not only</span>
  <span id="freeText2600364945225391301" style="display:none">The exceptionally talented and incredibly popular Raina Telgemeier returns with a sequel to her beloved Smile. This is the story of Raina and her little sister, Amara. Raina was desperate to have a little sister, but Amara is not working out the way she had pictured. Now Raina is stuck on a road trip with her sister, little brother and her mother. They are all stuck in a van traveling from San Francisco to Colorado for a family reunion. The relationship between the two sisters is tense, not only because they have very different personalities but also because they are both artists. Then you add in the clear issues of Raina’s parents and you have a dynamic view of a family on the brink of big changes. It’s just up to Raina and Amara as to how their relationship with one another will change.<br /><br />Telgemeier has created another breathtakingly honest graphic novel for elementary and middle grade readers. Through her illustrations and humor, she shows a family at the crux of a moment that could change things forever. The book though focuses on flashbacks showing the family and how relationships have altered. Readers may be so focused on the story of the two sisters that they too will be blindsided along with Raina about the other issues facing their family. It’s a craftily told story, one that surprises and delights.<br /><br />As always, Telgemeier’s art is fantastic. She has a light touch, one that invites readers into her world and her family and where they long to linger. Her art is always approachable and understandable, more about a vehicle to tell the story than about making an artistic statement on its own. It is warm, friendly and fantastic.<br /><br />Highly recommended, this book belongs in every library that works with children. A dynamite sequel that lives up to the incredible first book. Appropriate for ages 9-12.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2600364945225391301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6730406198209471683">I don't know what I expected when I got this book from the library, but it exceeded by expectations!<br/><br/>The first thing that you should know is that it isn't a regular novel. This is a comic. I was expected it to be like a regular book when I got it, and I thought it would be disappointing. But I decided to give it a go and I really liked it. <br/><br/>I could relate to many things in this book. The biggest thing was her relationship with her sister.   <span id="freeText6730406198209471683" style="display:none">I don't know what I expected when I got this book from the library, but it exceeded by expectations!<br /><br />The first thing that you should know is that it isn't a regular novel. This is a comic. I was expected it to be like a regular book when I got it, and I thought it would be disappointing. But I decided to give it a go and I really liked it. <br /><br />I could relate to many things in this book. The biggest thing was her relationship with her sister. I knew <b>EXACTLY</b> how she felt during the parts of the book when she was having a hard time with her younger sister. During the story they take a trip to Colorado in their van. They have fights along the way. When they get there Raina realizes that her cousins aren't how she remembered them. They ignore her and call her Penelope. <br /><br />This story is based on her real relationship with her sister. In the end her relationship with her sister is mended. She knows that they love each other even though they fight. I liked this story because it sticks to reality. No unicorns, wizards, just reality. <br /><br />I enjoyed how this story was clean of bad language and there was no potty humor.<br /><br />I recommend this book from 3rd grade and up. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1003171855" />
    <a title="Gary Anderson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2799121-gary-anderson"><img alt="Gary Anderson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586222637p2/2799121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1003171855?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary Anderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary Anderson" href="/user/show/2799121-gary-anderson">Gary Anderson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545749510" href="/book/show/17801394-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1003171855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11331551239885459126">Although it kept my attention, I couldn't quite get a handle on SISTERS. Raina Telgemeier's two previous graphic novels--SMILE and DRAMA--were satisfying stories, but this one seemed to be in search of what it was really about. Tied together by a family car trip, other episodes are juxtaposed to show how the sisters relate differently to what is going on around them. Young readers may connect with the various episodes involving cousins, pets, and the need to keep electronics fully charged, but I</span>
  <span id="freeText11331551239885459126" style="display:none">Although it kept my attention, I couldn't quite get a handle on SISTERS. Raina Telgemeier's two previous graphic novels--SMILE and DRAMA--were satisfying stories, but this one seemed to be in search of what it was really about. Tied together by a family car trip, other episodes are juxtaposed to show how the sisters relate differently to what is going on around them. Young readers may connect with the various episodes involving cousins, pets, and the need to keep electronics fully charged, but I thought SISTERS skimmed along too lightly on big issues involving family. To be completely honest, it's possible that my enjoyment was affected by the fact that the graphic novel e-galley I received was mostly in black-and-white, although the publisher included a note saying that the final version "will be in full color throughout." So, it was kind of like reading a novel with most of the adjectives removed. I hope to read the full color version after publication.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11331551239885459126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Iy0tZW8oXAGYc79jOclvc9eT5+lOWfQyNUnU6qLcMECDXGs+SVwNbOqGSXaPE69hLwo2Vas5Y1X1jOWTTyrKUw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
